27/06/2024, 22:18 - Kaelo: #include <avr/io.h>
#include <util/delay.h>

#define F_CPU 16000000UL // 16 MHz clock speed

// Define the correct passcode
const uint8_t correct_passcode[4] = {4, 3, 2, 1};

// Function prototypes
void init_ports(void);
void blink_bi_color_led(uint8_t color, uint8_t times);
uint8_t read_button(void);

int main(void)
{
    uint8_t input_sequence[4];
    uint8_t button_press_count = 0;

    // Initialize ports
    init_ports();

    while (1)
    {
        // Read button press
        uint8_t button = read_button();
        if (button != 0xFF) // A button was pressed
        {
            // Light corresponding LED on PORTC
            PORTC |= (1 << button);
            input_sequence[button_press_count] = button + 1; // Store button number (1-based)
            button_press_count++;

            // Check if 4 buttons have been pressed
            if (button_press_count == 4)
            {
                uint8_t correct = 1;
                for (uint8_t i = 0; i < 4; i++)
                {
                    if (input_sequence[i] != correct_passcode[i])
                    {
                        correct = 0;
                        break;
                    }
                }

                if (correct)
                {
                    // Blink green LED 4 times
                    blink_bi_color_led(0, 4);
                }
                else
                {
                    // Blink red LED 4 times
                    blink_bi_color_led(1, 4);
                }

                // Reset for next input sequence
                button_press_count = 0;
                PORTC = 0x00;
            }
        }
    }

    return 0;
}

void init_ports(void)
{
    // Set PORTB as input
    DDRB = 0x00;
    PORTB = 0xFF; // Enable pull-up resistors

    // Set PORTC as output
    DDRC = 0x0F;
    PORTC = 0x00;

    // Set PORTD as output
    DDRD = 0x03;
    PORTD = 0x00;
}

void blink_bi_color_led(uint8_t color, uint8_t times)
{
    for (uint8_t i = 0; i < times; i++)
    {
        if (color == 0)
        {
            // Blink green
            PORTD = (1 << PD0);
            _delay_ms(500);
            PORTD = 0x00;
            _delay_ms(500);
        }
        else
        {
            // Blink red
            PORTD = (1 << PD1);
            _delay_ms(500);
            PORTD = 0x00;
            _delay_ms(500);
        }
    }
}

uint8_t read_button(void)
{
    // Check each button on PORTB (PB0 to PB3)
    for (uint8_t i = 0; i < 4; i++)
    {
        if (!(PINB & (1 << i))) // Button is pressed (active low)
        {
            return i;
        }
    }

    return 0xFF; // No button pressed
}

28/06/2024, 07:30 - Mark: #include <avr/io.h>
#define F_CPU 1000000UL
#include <util/delay.h>
#include <stdint.h>
// activated when the pinis wrong
void blink_off();
//activated when the pin is correct
void blink_on();

int main(void)
{
	//outputs
	DDRC =0x0F;
	DDRD =(1<<PD0)|(1<<PD1);
	// enabling pull up resistor and inputs
	DDRB =0xF0;
	PORTB =0x0F;

	int password[4];
	int times =0;
	// password
	int checker[]={2,1,4,3};
	while(times<4){
		// reading the buttons pressed while recording them as password inputs
		int there;
		int read = PINB;
		if ((read&(1<<PB0))==0){
			PORTC |=(1<<PC0);
			there =1;
		}
		else{
			PORTC&=~(1<<PC0);
		}
		if((read&(1<<PB1))==0){
			PORTC|=(1<<PC1);
			there= 2;
		}
		else{
			PORTC&=~(1<<PC1);
		}
		if ((read&(1<<PB2))==0){
			PORTC|=(1<<PC2
			);
			there =3;
		}
		else{
			PORTC&=~(1<<PC2);
		}
		if((read&(1<<PB3))==0){
			PORTC|=(1<<PC3);
			there=4;
		}
		else{
			PORTC&=~(1<<PC3);
		}
		password[times]=there;
		// delay waiting for the next button to be pressed
		_delay_ms(12000);
		times ++;
		if(times>4){
			break;
		}
	}
	// checks the password
	
	for(int y=0;y<4;y++){
		if(checker[y]==password[y]){
			blink_on();
			break;
		}
		else{
			blink_off();
			break;
		}
	}
	

	
}

void blink_on(){
	for (int i =0;i<4;i++){
		PORTD |=(1<<PD0);
		PORTD &=(1<<PD0);
		_delay_ms(500);
		PORTD &=~(0x03);
		_delay_ms(500);
	}
	
}
void blink_off(){
	for(int r=0;r<4;r++){
		PORTD |=(1<<PD1);
		PORTD &=(1<<PD1);
		_delay_ms(500);
		PORTD =~(0x03);
		_delay_ms(500);
	}
}

void blink_off();

void blink_on();

int main(void)
{
	//outputs
	DDRC =0x0F;
	DDRD =0x0F;

	DDRB =0xF0;
	PORTB =0x0F;

	int password[4];
	int times =0;
	// password
	int checker[]={2,1,4,3};
	while(times<4){
		// reading the buttons pressed while recording them as password inputs
		int there; // is the variable that decodes the input pin
		int read = PINB;
		if ((read&(1<<PB0))==0){
			PORTC |=(1<<PC0);
			there =1;
		}
		else{
			PORTC&=~(1<<PC0);
		}
		if((read&(1<<PB1))==0){

		_delay_ms(500);

		_delay_ms(500);

		}
		else{
			PORTC&=~(1<<PC1);
		}
		if ((read&(1<<PB2))==0){
			PORTC|=(1<<PC2
			);
			there =3;
		}
		else{
			PORTC&=~(1<<PC2);
		}
		if((read&(1<<PB3))==0){
			PORTC|=(1<<PC3);
			there=4;
		}
		else{
			PORTC&=~(1<<PC3);
		}
		password[times]=there;
		// delay waiting for the next button to be pressed
		_delay_ms(12000);
		times ++;
		if(times>4){
			break;
		}
	}
	// checks the password and confirms if it is correct
	for(int y=0;y<4;y++){
		if(checker[y]==password[y]){
			blink_on();
			break;
		}
		else{
			blink_off();
			break;
		}
	}
}

void blink_on(){
	for (int i =0;i<4;i++){
		PORTD =1<<PD0;
		_delay_ms(500);
		PORTD ^=(1<<PD0);
		_delay_ms(500);
	}
	
}
void blink_off(){
	for(int r=0;r<4;r++){
		PORTD =1<<PD1;
		_delay_ms(500);
		PORTD ^=1<<PD1;
		_delay_ms(500);
	}
}

16/07/2024, 11:31 - Mark: To find the stress at 0Â°F and the temperature at which the stress would be zero, we'll use the concept of thermal stress. 

Thermal stress \(\sigma\) is given by the formula:

\[
\sigma = E \cdot \alpha \cdot \Delta T
\]

where:
- \(E\) is the Young's modulus (29 \(\times\) 10^6 psi)
- \(\alpha\) is the coefficient of thermal expansion (6.5 \(\times\) 10^-6 /Â°F)
- \(\Delta T\) is the change in temperature.

Let's calculate the stress at 0Â°F first. 

1. **Stress at 0Â°F:**

\[
\Delta T = T_{\text{initial}} - T_{\text{final}} = 70^\circ F - 0^\circ F = 70^\circ F
\]

\[
\sigma = E \cdot \alpha \cdot \Delta T = 29 \times 10^6 \, \text{psi} \cdot 6.5 \times 10^{-6} /^\circ F \cdot 70^\circ F
\]

\[
\sigma = 29 \times 10^6 \cdot 6.5 \times 10^{-6} \cdot 70
\]

\[
\sigma = 29 \cdot 6.5 \cdot 70 \text{ psi}
\]

\[
\sigma = 13195 \text{ psi}
\]

2. **Temperature at which the stress would be zero:**

For the stress to be zero, the thermal expansion must counteract the applied load.

The stress due to the applied load (\(\sigma_L\)) is:

\[
\sigma_L = \frac{P}{A} = \frac{1200 \text{ lb}}{0.25 \text{ in}^2} = 4800 \text{ psi}
\]

At equilibrium, the thermal stress must equal the stress due to the load:

\[
E \cdot \alpha \cdot \Delta T = \frac{P}{A}
\]

Solving for \(\Delta T\):

\[
\Delta T = \frac{\frac{P}{A}}{E \cdot \alpha} = \frac{4800 \text{ psi}}{29 \times 10^6 \text{ psi} \cdot 6.5 \times 10^{-6} /^\circ F}
\]

\[
\Delta T = \frac{4800}{29 \cdot 6.5}
\]

\[
\Delta T = \frac{4800}{188.5}
\]

\[
\Delta T \approx 25.47^\circ F
\]

So, the temperature change required to counteract the stress due to the load is approximately 25.47Â°F. Since the initial temperature is 70Â°F, the final temperature at which the stress would be zero is:

\[
T_{\text{final}} = T_{\text{initial}} - \Delta T = 70^\circ F - 25.47^\circ F \approx 44.53^\circ F
\]

### Summary:
- The stress at 0Â°F is approximately 13195 psi.
- The temperature at which the stress would be zero is approximately 44.53Â°F.

02/08/2024, 11:22 - Kaelo: #define F_CPU 16000000UL
#include <avr/io.h>
#include <avr/interrupt.h>
#include <util/delay.h>

char display[] = {0x3F, 0x06, 0x5B, 0x4F, 0x66, 0x6D, 0x7D, 0x07, 0x7F, 0x67};
int SEG1 = 4;
int SEG2 = 5;
int delayvalue = 5000;
int i = 0;
int j = 0;

/* A function to act as a persistence of vision delay */
void vision_persist(){
	int delay = delayvalue;
	while (0 < delay){
		_delay_us(1);
		--delay;
	}
}

/* A function to reload the timer initial value after the timer overflows */
void sevseg_refreshDisplay(){
	TCNT1L = 0x15; /* Load TCNT1, count for 30ms */
	TCNT1H = 0x9F;
	TCCR1B |= (1<<CS11); /* Start timer1 with 8 pre-scaler */
	TIMSK1 |= (1<<TOIE1); /* Enable Timer1 overflow interrupts */
}

void displayLED(int input){ /* Function to display a number on the LED */
	char BH = (~PORTB & 0xF0);
	char BL = (display[input] & 0x0F);
	PORTB = ~(BH|BL);
	char DL = (~PORTD & 0x0F);
	char DH = (display[input] & 0xF0);
	PORTD = ~(DH|DL);
}

ISR(TIMER1_OVF_vect){ /* Interrupt Service Routine for Timer1 */
	PORTB ^= (1<<SEG1); /* Toggle SEG1 */
	PORTB ^= (1<<SEG2); /* Toggle SEG2 */
	displayLED(i);
	vision_persist();
	PORTB ^= (1<<SEG1); /* Toggle SEG1 */
	PORTB ^= (1<<SEG2); /* Toggle SEG2 */
	displayLED(j);
	vision_persist();
	sevseg_refreshDisplay();
}

void initADC() {
	ADMUX = (1<<REFS0); // AVcc with external capacitor at AREF pin
	ADCSRA = (1<<ADEN) | (1<<ADPS2) | (1<<ADPS1) | (1<<ADPS0); // Enable ADC and set prescaler to 128
}

uint16_t readADC(uint8_t channel) {
	ADMUX = (ADMUX & 0xF8) | (channel & 0x07); // Select ADC channel
	ADCSRA |= (1<<ADSC); // Start conversion
	while(ADCSRA & (1<<ADSC)); // Wait for conversion to complete
	return ADC;
}

int main(void){
	DDRB |= 0xFF;
	DDRD |= 0xFF;
	PORTB |= (1<<SEG1);

	initADC();

	/***********************************************************************/
	/* Interrupt Setup */
	sevseg_refreshDisplay();
	sei(); /* Enable Global Interrupt */
	/***********************************************************************/
	
	while (1) {
		uint16_t adcValue = readADC(0); // Read ADC value from channel 0
		uint16_t mappedValue = (adcValue * 99L) / 1023; // Map ADC value to 0-99
		i = mappedValue / 10; // Tens place
		j = mappedValue % 10; // Ones place
		_delay_ms(50);
	}
}

30/10/2024, 11:14 - Kaelo: Yes, there are cars that donâ€™t use traditional camshafts. Some modern engines use **camless valve technology**, where the conventional camshaft is replaced with electronically controlled actuators. This allows for more precise control of valve timing, opening, and closing, which can improve efficiency, performance, and emissions.

### Examples of Camless Engine Technology
- **Koenigsegg Freevalve**: Koenigsegg developed a camless engine technology called "Freevalve," where the engine valves are controlled by pneumatic-hydraulic-electric actuators. This allows each valve to operate independently, eliminating the need for a camshaft and offering much finer control over the combustion process.
- **Fiat MultiAir**: Fiat developed the MultiAir system, which, while not fully camless, reduces reliance on the camshaft by using hydraulic actuators for the intake valves. This system improves fuel efficiency and engine responsiveness but still retains a camshaft for other engine functions.

### Advantages of Camless Engines
1. **Increased Efficiency**: Independent valve control allows for better air-fuel mixture management, resulting in improved fuel efficiency.
2. **Lower Emissions**: More precise control of valve timing can optimize combustion, leading to fewer emissions.
3. **Higher Performance**: With camless control, engines can achieve faster response times and potentially higher RPMs, making them more adaptable for performance needs.

Although fully camless engines are not yet widespread in production cars, they represent an exciting innovation in automotive engineering with potential benefits for efficiency and performance in future vehicles.

09/12/2024, 11:49 - Kaelo: To understand how the answer is derived, letâ€™s break down the equation and calculations step by step:

The equation given is:

\[
E_A = V_\phi - jX_s I_A
\]

### Key Parameters:
1. \( V_\phi = 208 \angle 0^\circ \, \text{V} \)  
2. \( X_s = 2.5 \, \Omega \)  
3. \( I_A = 27.4 \angle 36.87^\circ \, \text{A} \)  

---

### Step 1: Compute \( jX_s I_A \)

The term \( jX_s I_A \) represents the voltage drop due to the reactance.  
- Multiply the magnitude of \( X_s \) by \( I_A \):  
  \[
  X_s I_A = 2.5 \cdot 27.4 = 68.5 \, \text{V}
  \]
- The angle of \( jX_s I_A \) is shifted by \( 90^\circ \) due to the multiplication by \( j \):  
  \[
  \text{Angle of } jX_s I_A = 36.87^\circ + 90^\circ = 126.87^\circ
  \]
Thus:  
\[
jX_s I_A = 68.5 \angle 126.87^\circ \, \text{V}
\]

---

### Step 2: Subtract \( jX_s I_A \) from \( V_\phi \)

\[
E_A = V_\phi - jX_s I_A
\]

1. Represent \( V_\phi \) in rectangular form:  
   \[
   V_\phi = 208 \angle 0^\circ = 208 + j0 \, \text{V}
   \]

2. Represent \( jX_s I_A \) in rectangular form:  
   Convert \( 68.5 \angle 126.87^\circ \) to rectangular coordinates:  
   \[
   jX_s I_A = -68.5 \cos(126.87^\circ) + j(68.5 \sin(126.87^\circ))
   \]
   Using trigonometric values:  
   \[
   jX_s I_A = -40.5 + j54.8 \, \text{V}
   \]

3. Subtract \( jX_s I_A \) from \( V_\phi \):  
   \[
   E_A = (208 + j0) - (-40.5 + j54.8)
   \]
   Perform the subtraction:  
   \[
   E_A = 208 + 40.5 - j54.8
   \]
   \[
   E_A = 249.1 - j54.8 \, \text{V}
   \]

---

### Step 3: Convert \( E_A \) back to Polar Form

The magnitude of \( E_A \):  
\[
|E_A| = \sqrt{(249.1)^2 + (-54.8)^2}
\]
\[
|E_A| = \sqrt{62045.81 + 3004.04} = \sqrt{65049.85} \approx 255 \, \text{V}
\]

The angle of \( E_A \):  
\[
\theta = \tan^{-1}\left(\frac{-54.8}{249.1}\right)
\]
\[
\theta \approx -12.4^\circ
\]

Thus, in polar form:  
\[
E_A = 255 \angle -12.4^\circ \, \text{V}
\]

---

### Final Answer:
\[
E_A = 255 \angle -12.4^\circ \, \text{V}
\]
